  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f43b2a73-32f0-460f-99a0-2598bd77bc10'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18313699176404713915"><i>“You see, there is safety in simplicity… in a life of simple peace, where the electricity doesn’t dance across the backs of my eyelids, and the sparks don’t slither over my consciousness. Only asinine peace, where my paintings don’t seem to paint themselves, leaving me with terrible feelings of premonition and a chill beneath my fingernails.”</i><br/><br/><br/>Seraph Black used to think that</span>
  <span id="freeText18313699176404713915" style="display:none"><i>“You see, there is safety in simplicity… in a life of simple peace, where the electricity doesn’t dance across the backs of my eyelids, and the sparks don’t slither over my consciousness. Only asinine peace, where my paintings don’t seem to paint themselves, leaving me with terrible feelings of premonition and a chill beneath my fingernails.”</i><br /><br /><br />Seraph Black used to think that she was prepared for anything. She could last days without eating and she always walked away from the violent altercations with her father relatively unharmed. She survived working at the club and the drive to school every day in her mother’s rust-bucket of a car… but it all changed when Noah and Cabe came bulldozing into her life, careless of the precious secrets they picked apart in their quest to take over her world. She was even less prepared for the mysterious Miro and Silas, and nothing could have prepared her for the bond. The connection. The reason for it all.<br /> <br />Someone wanted her to stay away from her new friends, but she wasn’t willing to do that.<br /><br />Everyone had secrets.<br /><br />She wanted to <i>know</i> theirs. They wanted to <i>own</i> hers. <br /><br />And the stalker?<br /><br />He seemed to know everything already.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Siv, <br/><br/>Word of advice, don't count your chickens before they're hatched! I have it on good authority that the second half of Charcoal Tears is comple<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Siv, <br /><br />Word of advice, don't count your chickens before they're hatched! I have it on good authority that the second half of Charcoal Tears is complete, utter, rambling CRAP, so you don't need to stress about release dates for number 2 in the series. <br />Now that your expectations are dismally low, go back and enjoy the rest of the book :p <br />On a more serious note, thank you for reading it, and I hope you enjoy it!! I'll keep you updated on the release schedule via my blog. <br />Or telepathy. <br />Whichever is more reliable. <br />-Jane<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164943103" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164943103?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36271664-charcoal-tears">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=brs-done">brs-done</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164943103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3190306896518401141">I recently looked up the common methods of <a href='https://people.howstuffworks.com/cult4.htm' rel='nofollow noopener'>cult indoctrination</a> - on HowStuffWorks, because I have no class - and came to a chilling conclusion; <b>the Zevgheni are a cult, and Seph is in the process of joining. </b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511244452ra/24495395.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Every key step for indoctrinating a cult member (aka <b>thought reform</b>), listed in the linked article, is reflected in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36271664.Charcoal_Tears__Seraph_Black___1_' title='Charcoal Tears (Seraph Black, #1) by Jane Washington' rel='nofollow noopener'>Charcoal Tears</a>. See for yourself: <br/><br/>-<b> Step 1, Deception</b><i> - cults trick new members into joining by misleading them or withholding information about the true nature of the group; t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3190306896518401141" style="display:none">I recently looked up the common methods of <a href="https://people.howstuffworks.com/cult4.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">cult indoctrination</a> - on HowStuffWorks, because I have no class - and came to a chilling conclusion; <b>the Zevgheni are a cult, and Seph is in the process of joining. </b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511244452ra/24495395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every key step for indoctrinating a cult member (aka <b>thought reform</b>), listed in the linked article, is reflected in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36271664.Charcoal_Tears__Seraph_Black___1_" title="Charcoal Tears (Seraph Black, #1) by Jane Washington" rel="nofollow noopener">Charcoal Tears</a>. See for yourself: <br><br>-<b> Step 1, Deception</b><i> - cults trick new members into joining by misleading them or withholding information about the true nature of the group; they might even use a member's induced altered consciousness to increase vulnerability to suggestion.</i> The Adairs and Quillans repeatedly dodge questions, keeping Seph in the dark about her own nature and the truth of their bond. They definitely benefit from her vulnerability due to her abusive father and stalker since it helps them gain her trust. When Seph asks for information on the bond, so she can decide for herself if it's something she wants, this is the response she gets: <blockquote>
  <i>His expression hardened. "Do you trust us?"<br>I nodded, but I wasn't entirely sure.<br>"I understand that it's a lot to ask, Seph... to blindly trust people in a situation like this. But it's for your own good. We can't answer that question just yet - soon, but not just yet."</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511244452ra/24495396.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>- <b>Step 2, Isolation</b> - <i>Cults cut off members from the outside world. The members of the cult become the person's only social contact and feedback mechanism. Cults may not allow unsupervised contact with the "outside world."</i> From the moment Seph meets her pairs, she spends barely a moment outside of their company; if it were up to the boys she would probably never leave their side. <blockquote>
  <i>Cabe looked a little incensed. "We don't stalk her."<br>"If she didn't want to be friends, we probably would." Noah countered.<br>Cabe tilted his head, considering this. "Yeah, ok."</i>
</blockquote> Her old friend Matthew is cut from her life completely, even her brother Tariq barely sees her more than a few minutes at a time after she catches the Adair's attention. Case in point, after Seph receives a shock from her stalker and tries to tell Tariq: <blockquote>
  <i>"I should talk to Tariq too."<br>"No." Quillan brushed the hair from my face. "Sorry, Seph. Seeing you like this will only upset him."</i>
</blockquote>The boys are extremely protective of Seph, essentially cutting her off from the world.<br><br>- <b>Step 3, Induced Dependency </b>- <i>Cults demand absolute, unquestioning devotion, loyalty and submission. A cult member's sense of self is systematically destroyed. The leader typically controls every minute of a member's waking time. There is no free time to think or analyze. Members are told what to eat, what to wear, when to sleep ... the member is removed from all decision-making. </i> Within days of meeting the Adairs, Seph is living in their apartment, with her food, clothes, habits, and schedule all dictated by her new roommates. Because of the bond, she feels nauseous and unhappy whenever she isn't touching one of them. If that's not dependency, pray tell me what is. The pair seems to be designed to destroy independence. <br><br>- <b>Step 4, Dread </b>- <i>Once complete dependence is established, the member must retain the leader's good favor or else his life falls apart.</i> Here's where it gets tricky, because it may not seem as though Seph is at the mercy of the Adairs and Quillans. But think about it. Seph has been abused all her life and is in dire need of affection, trust, and a leadership figure. When a group of guys enters her life and seems to want to take care of her, of course she jumps at the chance; this dependency is only intensified by the pair bonds. Seph is so desperate for someone to follow and trust that she accepts anything the boys throw at her. When told that she isn't allowed to know facts about her own nature, she doesn't question it. When told to stay in the Adairs' apartment for ten days straight, Seph doesn't even blink. Clearly she will do anything she's told. <br>What would happen if she fell out of favor with the boys? Seph has shown that she is protective of them - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Noah and Cabe were threatened she exploded and killed their attacker <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. At the slightest hint that the bond may not be completed between her and her men, she has a full breakdown. Clearly her emotional stability depends on her relationship with them. <br><br><br>This all looks very bad for our heroes. <b>We should have trouble romanticizing a relationship with such creepy undertones.</b> Noah and Cabe fully admit to stalking Seph in the middle of the book - how can that be construed as romantic when the main villain is also a stalker, albeit a much more sinister one? How come everybody still swoons at the thought of Silas, Miro, Noah, and Cabe?<br><br>There's an explanation for that:<br>The <b><a href="http://how-i-met-your-mother.wikia.com/wiki/The_Dobler-Dahmer_Theory" rel="nofollow noopener">Dobler/Dahmer Theory</a>.</b> See: How I Met Your Mother, S08E15<br>In the show, one of Ted's girlfriends illegally sets off a fire alarm (among other things) to meet him. Ted's friends call her crazy; Ted calls her romantic because he was into the gesture. <blockquote>
  <i>"If both people are into each other, then a big romantic gesture works: Dobler. But if one person isn't into the other, the same gesture comes off serial-killer crazy: Dahmer."</i>
</blockquote> While objectively the heroes might look like crazy cult members attempting to indoctrinate an abused, vulnerable girl into their Zevgheni group, one important factor changes the game: sexual attraction. The truth is, Seraph totally digs the whole experience. She loves the attention and the racy steamy moments. So <b>is it really wrong to indoctrinate someone if they're enjoying the hell out of it? </b><br><br>Debatable. <br><br>I'm coming down on the Dahmer side; I still think Seph's developing relationship is unhealthy and really sketchy. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511244860ra/24495411.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But I know I'm in the minority, so I plan on continuing the series to see if something will change my mind.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3190306896518401141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15296909346861582066"><b>FREE! July 1, 2019 on US Kindle.</b> I am in the Seraph Black bubble forever. #eatallthecake<br/><br/>FIRST READ NOVEMBER 2017: ★★★★★<br/>SECOND READ JULY 2018: ★★★★★<br/><br/>New thoughts: OMG the LURVE is still strong and filled with many ALL CAPS. All I can say is that it awakens my inner Twilight fangirl. I love the boys, I love Seraph, I love EVERYTHING. It's similar to that magic I felt when I first read the Fever series, discovered Eric Northman from the Sookie books, and... Twilight. On to re-reading book two!<br/><br/><b>origin</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15296909346861582066" style="display:none"><b>FREE! July 1, 2019 on US Kindle.</b> I am in the Seraph Black bubble forever. #eatallthecake<br><br>FIRST READ NOVEMBER 2017: ★★★★★<br>SECOND READ JULY 2018: ★★★★★<br><br>New thoughts: OMG the LURVE is still strong and filled with many ALL CAPS. All I can say is that it awakens my inner Twilight fangirl. I love the boys, I love Seraph, I love EVERYTHING. It's similar to that magic I felt when I first read the Fever series, discovered Eric Northman from the Sookie books, and... Twilight. On to re-reading book two!<br><br><b>original review:</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510156831ra/24392952.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THIS BOOK. Yes, it's Young Adult and I am an old lady. Guess what???<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510156831ra/24392954.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And the Adairs and Quillens are MINE. Yes, I know the Adairs are 17 years old (Cabe and Noah), but when I read them, I am fulfilling my Twilight Bella Swan fangirl side, so it's OKAY. Don't judge!<br><br>The Quillens are only 25 which makes me almost 20 years older then them, but again: don't judge. This is my fantasy world. Okay, maybe it's not JUST mine. Just kidding. Stay away from my boys!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510156831ra/24392955.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, seriously though. Review time.<br><br>This book is about a Mary Sue Super Special Snowflake with powerful abilities who just happens to be like the soul mates.... of FOUR guys. They are her magical "pairs" and complete her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510156832ra/24392956.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's love/lust at first sight and they are inseparable by day one. So unrealistic and over the top and I LOVED IT!<br><br>Seraph (that name, right) has an ability where she can use or create electricity and zap people or even blow stuff up (called valcrick)! She lives with her brother, Zariq, and their abusive father. Seraph is a loner at school; quiet, keeps her head down, doesn't have friends. Until she meets her boys.<br><br>Then, she starts to smile and open up. She also has another special ability: she draws future events. This ability is tied to her other "pair" - the Quillens. Silas is the grumpy, reclusive, dangerous bad boy, and Miro is the controlled, responsible but calming one - and also her art teacher! haha<br><br>We see the beginning of a new world, filled with other people who have these abilities, called <i>Zevgheri</i>. Some can control fire or people's minds, etc. They are controlled by the <i>Klovoda,</i> who are sort of like a magic seedy underworld mafia who sometimes make other Zevs do secret jobs for them.<br><br>There is no sex in this but I loved how Seraph got to have 4 boys/men of her own and the <b>reverse harem</b> trope is da bomb! My favorite! I love when she gets <i>"strained"</i> because of their bond and the guys have to touch her and be near her to calm it down! HAHAHAHA - that is just awesome. <br><br>Already reading book 2, it was so good...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510156831ra/24392953.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1402332511" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1402332511" />
    <a title="Pao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12593547-pao"><img alt="Pao" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505516126p2/12593547.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1402332511?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pao" href="/user/show/12593547-pao">Pao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Pao by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/17688800-siv-therese">Siv Therese</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1402332511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3273342850897029992">I'll start of by saying that I don't intend to offend the author or anyone who has read the book and liked it. <br/><br/><u>This is my opinion.</u> <br/><br/>As this is my opinion, I'm going to speak the truth about what I think. <br/><br/>Summed up in one image:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444154051i/16460190._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Charcoal Tears</i> felt like reading a damn copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/122683' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Academy Series by C.L. Stone</a>.<br/><br/>That's the ugly truth.<br/><br/>It's not the same word by word, but there are TOO MANY "similarities" existing between one and the other and you cannot expect me not to point them out when I've read The </span>
  <span id="freeText3273342850897029992" style="display:none">I'll start of by saying that I don't intend to offend the author or anyone who has read the book and liked it. <br><br><u>This is my opinion.</u> <br><br>As this is my opinion, I'm going to speak the truth about what I think. <br><br>Summed up in one image:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444154051i/16460190._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Charcoal Tears</i> felt like reading a damn copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/122683" rel="nofollow noopener">The Academy Series by C.L. Stone</a>.<br><br>That's the ugly truth.<br><br>It's not the same word by word, but there are TOO MANY "similarities" existing between one and the other and you cannot expect me not to point them out when I've read The Academy books before. <br><br>I'm not going to be a hypocrite denying that that was not one of the main reasons why I wanted to read Charcoal Tears. I'm a fan of The Academy and of course I'd like to read books alike. But I wasn't expecting this.<br><br>As I don't see the book listed as a re-telling, or <i>based on</i>, or <i>a fanfiction of</i>; and as I spent, if not not all, but most of the reading time comparing them both, I dare to say that it was like reading a copy.<br><br>I'll list my reasons:<br>►The Academy- Sang Sorenson is a 15 year old girl living with her father, mother <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[step-mom actually <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and sister. Sang is physically and verbally abused by her mother, forced to be isolated and this behaviour is neglected by the other two members of her family.<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Seraph is a 17 year old girl living with her father and brother. She's physically, verbally and, as she mentioned it, sexually abused by her father. Forced to work to be able to support her family. Luckyly, her brother is not indifferent to her situation. (This reminds me more of Kayli Winchester from the Scarab Beetle Series, which are also Academy books).<br><br>►The Academy- Sang meets 9 guys who belong to a secret organization named The Academy. They are grouped as a family/team:<br>-Mr. Blackbourne (connection with The Academy)<br>-Dr. Green (connection with The Academy)<br>-Kota (team leader)<br>-North<br>-Victor<br>-Nathan<br>-Silas<br>-Luke<br>-Gabriel<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Seraph meets only 4 guys, whom are <i>Zhevghéri</i> (?). From what I understood, they're people with some kind of powers.<br>-Mr. Quillan (the...boss)<br>-<b>Silas</b> <s>smooth</s> (Mr. Quillan's twin)<br>-Noah<br>-Cabe<br><br><b>To me</b>, these 4 guys are a strange combination of the 9 Academy guys. If you haven't read The Academy, you won't understand what I mean. But if you have, tell me if I'm wrong:<br>-Mr. Quillan= a bit of Mr. Blackbourne, Kota and Dr. Green together.<br>-Silas= Mr. Blackbourne + North<br>-Noah= a mix of Silas and Nathan<br>-Cabe= Victor + Gabriel + Luke<br><br>The same just in a smaller package.<br><br>►The Academy- Sang can identify each one of them by their smell or cologne.<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Surprinsigly, Seraph also does this. Only with Cabe <s>who smells like toffee (?)</s> and Quillan.<br><br>►The Academy- Sang and the guys have a nickname for each other, except for Mr. Blackbourne and Dr. Green (kind of):<br>Mr. Blackbourne/Miss Sorenson<br>Dr. Green or Sean/Pookie<br>Kota (not official yet)-10/52, but he calls her sweetie and sweetheart a lot<br>North-North star/Sang baby<br>Victor-Mr. Victor (not official yet)/Princess<br>Nathan-Honey/Peanut<br>Silas (not official yet)- Superman/ <b>
  <i>Aggele or aggele mou</i>
</b> (greek for "angel" or "my angel") <br>Luke (not official yet)-Always/Forever, meanwhile she's cupcake, sugar, sweetie, etc.<br>Gabriel-Meanie/Trouble<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Guess what? Seraph also has nicknames for her guys. Although I don't remember if for all of them:<br>Mr. Quillan-Mr. Bossman/not a name but he also calls her sweetheart, a lot.<br>Cabe-Lucifer/ ? <br>Noah-?/little ghost<br><br>Now, the least subtle "coincidence" between these books, Silas’ nickname for Seraph: <b>Angel</b>.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444168568ra/16461456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don't care if Seraph means angel. #notcooldude<br><br>►The Academy- Sang has <i>a thing</i> with each one of the guys. A gesture or action just for the two of them. Like rubbing noses with Kota, love bites with North or finger bitting with Nathan. They also give her small tokens, like a bracelet from Victor or the wrist band from Silas.<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- My interpretation of ↑ in this book, is what they call the <i>girlfriend insurance</i>. Seraph takes Quillans watch, Silas gets a tatoo that will be finished when he gets a girlfriend (because that's smart), Noah asks Seraph to get a piercieng and she's like <i>yeah, sure. I'll do it</i> (WTF?????), and I honestly don't remember what was Cabe's request but I bet something equally stupid.<br><br>►The Academy- On the third book of the series, Victor, Gabriel and Nathan take Sang on a shopping trip to the mall. <br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Cabe takes Seraph on a shopping trip to the mall. She feels like his ho (her words, not mine).<br><br>►The Academy- Sang has a stalker: Volto. He has followed her, taken pictures of her. Not sure if he's the one who plants fake bomb threats on her school.<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Seraph also has a stalker: The Messenger. He obviously follows her and has taken pictures of her. He planted a bomb on her school.<br><br>►The Academy- Sang gets notes from random guys on her classes but she never reads them because The Academy guys always intercept them.<br><br>▷Charcoal Tears- Seraph gets notes from random guys on her classes, she reads one but now the <i>Zhevghéri</i> guys intercept them.<br><br>Some other things that might seem dumb but I have to complain about:<br><br>●Sang has chameleon hair- Seraph has chameleon shoes.<br>●Victor has <i>fire eyes</i>- Cabe has <i> toffee eyes</i> (?)<br>●Mr. Blackbourne is Sang’s violin teacher- Mr. Quillan is Seraph’s art teacher<br>●Sang has a guy (Gabriel) who likes to dress her- Seraph has Clarin, a gay guy who obviously has to dress her.<br>●Academy guys keep secrets from Sang- <i>Zhevghéri</i> guys keep secrets from Seraph<br>●Academy guys go on secret jobs- <i>Zhevghéri</i> guys , yep, they go on secret jobs too<br>●Academy guys ground Sang- <i>Zhevghéri</i> guys ground Seraph<br>●Academy guys agree to keep things only in a platonic way with Sang- <i>Zhevghéri</i> guys “draw the line” about anything romantic with Seraph<br><br>I’m sorry if I simply couldn’t overlook all of that. I'm an Academy nerd.<br><br><i>*deep breath*</i><br><br>Those are not the only reasons why I simply couldn't love the book. The fantasy element is too weak. They are <i>Zhevghéri</i> , but what in the world is that? Why do they have powers? Why Seraph has two abilities and two marks? Why do they have to be paired? <br><br>It was a typical YA book: romance, flirting, high school, drama and almost no fantasy.<br><br>Seraph is...strange. She has no friends, she suddenly meets these two guys and starts hanging out with them, she gets comfortable too soon walking in and out of their apartment as if she owned it, wearing their clothes, gets a sassy attitude and craves for their touch...who changes that fast?<br><br>Then they say one day <i>"Hey, yo, Seph! We're moving to some magical city where our people lives"</i><br><br>Seph: okay!<br><br><i>"But your brother will stay here"</i><br><br>Seph: that's fine!<br><br><i>"One day you and all of us will be paired"</i><br><br>Seph: sure!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444180678ra/16463694.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The guys are <i>real</i> charmers:<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You're a miracle, Seraph. You're incredible. You just don't know it yet. Now get the hell out of my classroom"<br><br>"Don't think like that about yourself, Seph. Even if you hadn't been one of us, we still have stalked you to the grave"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1392327674ra/8539395.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m done. I needed to say it.<br><br>P.S. I'm so sorry I couldn't love this one, Siv :/</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

Screw you Washington. <br><br><b> Also, there's just no story here.... </b><br>- it's not like we've got a whole complex interesting world within the normal world, the Zevs or anything. <br>- It's not like there's so much backstory and thought gone into the whole damn series.... at all. <br>- It's not like the author writes beautifully and packed with enough action and intrigue to keep your interest throughout the whole 4 book series. <br>- It's not like the side characters are well thought out and beautiful funny characters in their own rights. *Coughs* Poison &amp; Clarin *coughs* <br><br><b> Who would wanna read this shit? </b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490597542i/22325483._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> So if you haven't worked it out, by the fact my review is actually rated 5 stars and the fact this is all crazy bullshit, this is satire.         rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26815771-charcoal-tears">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7331551-alex?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7331551-alex?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7331551-alex?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7331551-alex?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2194558612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15913281443579126086">No thanks. <br/>I'm so disappointed after reading all those raving reviews, and I'm obviously the odd man out, but I absolutely hated this book and the characters. I'm actually angry I finished it and didn't just DNF like I should have.<br/> I'm trying not to write an ugly review, but I have to say I need more world building and character development. The MC just annoyed me to death, but, to others this could be the best book they will ever read, so good luck if you try it. I'm defiantly skipping this ser</span>
  <span id="freeText15913281443579126086" style="display:none">No thanks. <br />I'm so disappointed after reading all those raving reviews, and I'm obviously the odd man out, but I absolutely hated this book and the characters. I'm actually angry I finished it and didn't just DNF like I should have.<br /> I'm trying not to write an ugly review, but I have to say I need more world building and character development. The MC just annoyed me to death, but, to others this could be the best book they will ever read, so good luck if you try it. I'm defiantly skipping this series though. <br />It's so sad because I really enjoy Jane Washingtons writing style and other series, so I'm chalking it up to being me, maybe I'm not built for characters like these and the "it's me not you" might work for this series. <br />Anyways, don't let my bad experience deter you, flavors of books are different for everyone, this series just might be your chunky monkey :) Happy reading. </span>

  <span id="freeText151804672186241472" style="display:none">Well the strangest thing happened when I finished the book and stopped to give my rating - a flock of flying pigs flew past my window (say that five times fast), I just realised I had just given a 4 star rating to a YA book AAAAAAAARGHHH!!!<br />Yes it's true a real 4 star rating who would have believed this day would happen, certainly not me.   <span id="freeText11532742270888239282" style="display:none"><b>Here's YOUR chance to WIN one of SEVEN eCopies from Jane Washington!<br><a href="http://tometender.blogspot.com/2015/10/jane-washingtons-charcoal-tears-blitz.html" rel="nofollow noopener"><img alt="http://tometender.blogspot.com/2015/10/jane-washingtons-charcoal-tears-blitz.html" height="298" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445262655i/16622599.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>International - Click on Banner to Enter! - Ends November 2, 2015</b><br><br>Meet Seraph Black. She’s a survivor, she’s proven it, time and again. Just stay calm, stay under the radar and keep surviving, not always easy, but it works, or at least it had until her world changes with just the screech of some tires. Cue the music, backlighting and action…two of the most overpowering and handsome teens to ever grace her school have arrived, and they make it their mission to stick to Seraph like white on rice. Noah and Cabe are larger than life, hotter than Hades and they know more about Seraph’s secrets than she does, perhaps because they have secrets of their own? What of Miro and Silas? With their own air of power and mystery, they too are part of Seraph’s new world, a world where Seraph is being stalked, threatened and spied on, a world where her very privacy becomes fodder for the school gossip mills. Who is out to get Seraph? Why? Is it because of the mysterious power of her paintings? What do they know that she doesn’t and why do they want to kill her?<br><br>Enter Seraph’s world, meet “the boys” and discover who and what Seraph is, right along with her. <b>Charcoal Tears</b> by Jane Washington is like falling through the rabbit hole into a deadly encounter in another world unknown to humans and it was hard to leave behind when the last page was finished. Visualize the world through Seraph’s eyes, see her struggle to believe in and accept that she needs these guys as much as they need her, but is her real Prince Charming among them? Are they all her champions in their own way? Will they keep her safe and destroy the stalker before it’s too late or will they find this veiled evil too powerful to destroy?<br><br>When the story teller is this brilliant, this creative and knows how to “set the hook” this well, there is always room for another great YA fantasy! All hail the level-headed heroine, the lack of whiny angst and of course, the hot heroes! Jane Washington is setting the bar high for herself, with clever dialogue, a hint of humor, shrouded threats and an entirely new race to learn about. I have the feeling the ending will torture me until I get my hands on the next book in this series.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599675285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7317309146947105935">Cliffhanger ending. <br/><br/>DNF disliked the protagonist. She's a 17 year old artist who is dense, gullible, weak, has low self esteem, is socially awkward, painfully shy, lacks self preservation & common sense I could go on but I'm sure my point was made. She has no redeemable personality traits. She's supposedly beautiful, magically gifted with 2 rare abilities, & every hot guy (that matters) wants her so of course every female hates her. She’s so special she doesn't just get paired with 2 guys but 4.</span>
  <span id="freeText7317309146947105935" style="display:none">Cliffhanger ending. <br /><br />DNF disliked the protagonist. She's a 17 year old artist who is dense, gullible, weak, has low self esteem, is socially awkward, painfully shy, lacks self preservation &amp; common sense I could go on but I'm sure my point was made. She has no redeemable personality traits. She's supposedly beautiful, magically gifted with 2 rare abilities, &amp; every hot guy (that matters) wants her so of course every female hates her. She’s so special she doesn't just get paired with 2 guys but 4. <br />The 4 H in this story felt one dimensional &amp; I disliked the fact they're unbearably bossy. <br />The story was an exercise in reader frustration &amp; incredibly juvenile considering 2 of the 4 guys paired with her are 25. Hot mess, even for a YA it was particularly annoying. I wouldn't Recommend this to anyone I liked. 1 star so glad it was free.</span>

<div id="review_2212255458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212255458" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212255458?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36271664-charcoal-tears">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-machalo-2017">br-machalo-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-machalo">br-machalo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212255458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14621608390964821684"><b>Buddy read with the MacHalo.</b><br/><br/>I can't believe I'm so affected by a YA novel. What the hell is happening with me? I mean it's not just an YA, it's one of many YA I read and liked in the past few months. <br/><br/>I can't properly express my feelings about this book mainly because I don't really understand them. I thought that if give myself some time and start the second book things will clear out a bit but now as I approach the end of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36271679.Watercolour_Smile__Seraph_Black___2_' title='Watercolour Smile (Seraph Black, #2) by Jane Washington' rel='nofollow noopener'>Watercolour Smile</a> I'm even more confused. And I have this heavy feeling i</span>
  <span id="freeText14621608390964821684" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with the MacHalo.</b><br /><br />I can't believe I'm so affected by a YA novel. What the hell is happening with me? I mean it's not just an YA, it's one of many YA I read and liked in the past few months. <br /><br />I can't properly express my feelings about this book mainly because I don't really understand them. I thought that if give myself some time and start the second book things will clear out a bit but now as I approach the end of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36271679.Watercolour_Smile__Seraph_Black___2_" title="Watercolour Smile (Seraph Black, #2) by Jane Washington" rel="nofollow noopener">Watercolour Smile</a> I'm even more confused. And I have this heavy feeling inside my chest that usually means I'm in for some real pain once the series is over. <br /><br />Seraph is not the kind of heroine I usually love. She's mostly a weak and dependant girl, except when she bursts into a magnificent fighter. But those are rare moments. And the male leads (yes as in multiple leads) take advantage of her passive side. Of her need to be loved and cherished. Something that's been denied her all her life. Throw in a really sick stalker and the poor girl is truly lost. I mean I would probably do whatever the people that 1) are my only friends and the only people showing interest in me and 2) are the ones protecting me from the psycho yet alone a poor abused teen. The secrecy is what's driving me nuts. Because I honestly don't believe it will help Seraph. I'm willing, however, to admit that the men probably do think it's for her good. If I didn't this would have been a rage review about how literature is normalizing control-freak behaviours when the man is both rich and handsome. And don't kid yourself, this book does precisely that. But it managed to captivate me and make me root for that twisted little poly-to-be group. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14621608390964821684" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1534651500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1534651500" />
    <a title="Abbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26781996-abbie"><img alt="Abbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473534398p2/26781996.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1534651500?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie" href="/user/show/26781996-abbie">Abbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26781996-abbie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26781996-abbie?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26781996-abbie?shelf=broken-home">broken-home</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26781996-abbie?shelf=powers">powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26781996-abbie?shelf=soul-mates">soul-mates</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1534651500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15865189059662984200">This is one of the most frustrating books I have ever read. I don't even fully understand the backstory! To briefly sum up this book is about Seraph, a girl who's grown up in a severely broken home with her little brother and abusive father. Then two new boys (Cabe and Noah) start school and basically attach themselves to her, acting all mysterious and protective/possessive. Oh and lets not forget Silas - the intense, brooding guy who hangs around at Seraph's work - and his twin brother Miro... </span>
  <span id="freeText15865189059662984200" style="display:none">This is one of the most frustrating books I have ever read. I don't even fully understand the backstory! To briefly sum up this book is about Seraph, a girl who's grown up in a severely broken home with her little brother and abusive father. Then two new boys (Cabe and Noah) start school and basically attach themselves to her, acting all mysterious and protective/possessive. Oh and lets not forget Silas - the intense, brooding guy who hangs around at Seraph's work - and his twin brother Miro... her art teacher. Seraph has a weird paranormal bond to all four of them and I can't quite figure out if they're all supposed to be her boyfriend or if it's just one?<br /><br />The boys/men firmly established themselves in her life and made it very clear to her that they knew more about Seraph's powers and the mysterious bond between them but they refused to tell her <b>
  <i>anything</i>
</b>. Of course Seraph didn't push them for answers - but hey, it's not like they took over a good portion of her life, making decisions for her, treating her like she's made out of glass... oh wait... That's what annoyed me so much, Seraph never demanded answers therefore we didn't find out what was actually going on until the end of the book, even then it's still patchy!<br /><br />Saying all that, I didn't hate this book I just found it really, <i>really</i> frustrating. The five-way romance kind of intrigued me (at times) although it also left me very confused. In general I'm leaning towards disliking this book a lot more than I liked it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15865189059662984200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3051401415" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17171938687534336510">I'm sitting here reading other reviews praising this book and I'm wondering if I read the same one?<br/><br/>I had high expectations. If you like super special snowflakes, this will be for you. I also missed that this was YA. I will now temper my expectations and not expect a lot of those sexy moments that I have grown to love in RH.<br/><br/>Please don't use my rating to decide if you want to read this or not. My three friends that I buddy read this with gave it 4 and 5's. This was just me. I can't think of a sing</span>
  <span id="freeText17171938687534336510" style="display:none">I'm sitting here reading other reviews praising this book and I'm wondering if I read the same one?<br /><br />I had high expectations. If you like super special snowflakes, this will be for you. I also missed that this was YA. I will now temper my expectations and not expect a lot of those sexy moments that I have grown to love in RH.<br /><br />Please don't use my rating to decide if you want to read this or not. My three friends that I buddy read this with gave it 4 and 5's. This was just me. I can't think of a single thing that I liked. Seraph and I did not click.. like at all. She was weak, vulnerable, was actually described as acting like a mouse. Reading about these type of female characters make me want to throw something. There were too many plot holes for me to ignore. The only characters that pose any interest to me are Silas and The Messenger. <br /><br />I'm buddy reading the whole series with my friends so I'm not tapping out. I already have started on book 2. Stay tuned!</span>

<div id="review_1789165044" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1789165044" />
    <a title="⋆☆☽ Kriss ☾☆⋆" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6497707-kriss"><img alt="⋆☆☽ Kriss ☾☆⋆" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517802332p2/6497707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1789165044?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⋆☆☽ Kriss ☾☆⋆" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⋆☆☽ Kriss ☾☆⋆" href="/user/show/6497707-kriss">⋆☆☽ Kriss ☾☆⋆</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36271664-charcoal-tears">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6497707-kriss?shelf=owned-kindle-books">owned-kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6497707-kriss?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6497707-kriss?shelf=arc-or-review-copy-books">arc-or-review-copy-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1789165044" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15195690584474869011">You know, while this book does have a few points I felt could have been better executed (I’ll discuss further down), I overall found this book to be an example of why I usually quite like the indie books I come across. Though it’s evident this author isn’t the most polished and probably didn’t have a massive editing team behind her to make all the rough edges glimmer, I still see ample talent from her and overall have good impressions of her from this book. <br/><br/>What drew me into this book was that t</span>
  <span id="freeText15195690584474869011" style="display:none">You know, while this book does have a few points I felt could have been better executed (I’ll discuss further down), I overall found this book to be an example of why I usually quite like the indie books I come across. Though it’s evident this author isn’t the most polished and probably didn’t have a massive editing team behind her to make all the rough edges glimmer, I still see ample talent from her and overall have good impressions of her from this book. <br /><br />What drew me into this book was that the blurb was so vague and the book takes its sweet time building up and slowly revealing things (though, I will say this now, this book cuts off a bit like a serial does, so I imagine that books 2-4 will all flow and cut off in a similar way to a serialization, rather than a traditional book format where a major conflict is resolved in book 1, leaving another for book 2, and so on until the end). For a lot of the book, the reader is left with a lot of questions. We’re never given the full picture, just enough pieces to keep us interested and able to follow the story. We’re teased with things like an obsessed stalker we come to know as “The Messenger” and an original fantasy-race; it becomes easy for the reader to begin wondering just who Seraph Black is and what’s going to happen to her. It takes a while before we start getting a clear idea of things, which might be a deal-breaker for some, who like having a general idea of the way the plot will develop before starting a book. If you’re okay with sort of being adrift in a book with slow reveals, this will suit you fine, but if vagueness and uncertainty are turn offs this book won’t get good until the last 20-30%<br /><br />I was impressed with the prose; it can be very poetic at times. Seraph is an interesting POV because of her inner thoughts. Overall, I noticed no real errors, though the ebook format wasn’t as nice as I’d like (skipped lines between paragraphs instead of idents, for example). As for context, I noted nothing especially problematic, though I am still a bit bothered by the 17 year old and the two 25 year olds. That is not an acceptable age gap. Men that old should have zero romantic and/or sexual interest in a teenager, which is pretty much the vibe you get from their interactions; there’s nothing beyond kissing and looking at a birthmark on her chest, but you still get a sense of the vibes going on. Sorry but your brain isn’t fully developed until you’re in your 20s there’s an immense maturity gap there. It’d be different if she was 19 or 20 but for a teenager even just a year is still a very long time of emotional and mental growth.<br /><br />My one other point of contention is that Seraph is pretty mellow and accepting of how Cabe and Noah just show up and, not only insert themselves into her life, but slowly begin having more influence and control over it. She has a few moments where she questions things “this is weird, right?” but after only knowing them for a few days they behave as if they’ve known each other for years. The brothers’ behaviors are very familiar and Seraph doesn’t ever seem to confront them about their behaviors or have the level of skepticism and internal conflict I’d expect from a girl who seems to have lived a life where she keeps everyone away and trusts very little so she can survive. The plot device of her just so easily accepting them into her life within the span of a week feels rather unnatural, like Seraph should have a much healthier fear of strangers and be more willing to question and offer resistance; she just goes along with what they do and say and only a few times wonders why she’s doing that, why she feels differently about them. Her easy acceptance of everything just seems too convenient for the plot. At the very least, the brothers should have been written as more slyly inserting themselves into her life over time, rather than just one day sideling up to her and behaving like they’re all best friends who have crossed all those aspects of human social interaction off their list and are fully comfortable with a well-established relationship.<br /><br />Outside of this, however, I found the ideas behind this story pretty interesting. I’ve not really seen the idea of a reverse harem in western literature, or if it’s done the concept of polyamory isn’t explored, and it’s usually very obvious who The One or the few main who form the love triangle/square/etc. will be, with the others just existing as side and stock characters as the apparent potentials turn into rivals. In this story, Seraph seems to hold affection for all four of the men and there’s no clear One of the bunch whom she values far more than anyone else, though I did get the impression that perhaps Silas holds a very special place in Seraph’s mind. It’s an interesting change. The romance aspect of this book was a little lacking, there’s no grand professing or sweet moments, just some kissing and general emotional connecting, but I think that this just means there’s going to be a slower build up to it, rather than having “the bond” explain away the “insta-love,” which sort of ruins the appeal of reading a romance since all the buildup that makes it real is condensed to “well they are bonded so that’s that now they’re all in love and together and it’s good.” <br /><br />The choice to create a unique fantasy race with its own society/system/etc. was an interesting move that I feel paid off. I’m interested to learn more about them and how everything functions and about how Seraph and her four partners fit into this world and the ministrations not yet known. This book only touches upon the larger things in motion, like the Adair’s father and the groups at the top of the society, with the focus being more on Seraph developing a connection with our four heros, so I look forward to an expansion of plot in book #2, which I have every intention of reading in the very near future.<br /><br />Overall, I feel like this was a surprisingly good YA book. It isn’t without its flaws, but overall I was engaged, interested, and eager to find out what happened next as I read each page. I recommend it to those who can tolerate vagueness that gives a slight air of mystery, but likes the realm of YA and doesn’t mind the idea that the heroine might end up romantically involved with four people. I’m quite happy with this read even in spite of my criticisms.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15195690584474869011" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer17956259899122829036"><i> This book is a torture device in the best and the worst way! </i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309372.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u> Disclaimer: I will admit I went ahead and read the 2nd book too before writing this review so I will try to keep it as separate as possible. </u><br/><br/>I am so confused as to how I am planning to rate this. So I will follow many of my fellow reviewers and break this down into the good and the bad and rate it after. Before that..<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309377.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309374.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481733578ra/21450104.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309373.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>ok one more<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406663355ra/10580484.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u> <b> That was for my new found love for polyamorous relationships. </b> </u><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309378.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b> The Good: Concept/Plot </b><br/>I discovered a new</span>
  <span id="freeText17956259899122829036" style="display:none"><i> This book is a torture device in the best and the worst way! </i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309372.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u> Disclaimer: I will admit I went ahead and read the 2nd book too before writing this review so I will try to keep it as separate as possible. </u><br><br>I am so confused as to how I am planning to rate this. So I will follow many of my fellow reviewers and break this down into the good and the bad and rate it after. Before that..<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309374.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481733578ra/21450104.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309373.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>ok one more<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406663355ra/10580484.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u> <b> That was for my new found love for polyamorous relationships. </b> </u><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490390174ra/22309378.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b> The Good: Concept/Plot </b><br>I discovered a new concept within this book of <i> Pairs </i> and their powers as well a whole secret society structure that the author introduced to us. It doesn't reach the far end spectrum of paranormal but it keeps you guessing as the it is definitely not completely normal either. <br><br><b> The Bad: Concept/Plot </b><br>As original as the author is within her writing style and plot devices, I felt she left too many plot holes trying to prolong the mystery or her series. It lead to a feeling of incompleteness within the story, I did not see any conclusion or explanation for the better part of the story which left us with many questions as a reader.<br><br><b> The Good: Writing </b><br>Jane has a talent! She is without a doubt one of the most compelling authors that I have read, she does wonders with suspense. She constantly had me on my feet eagerly guessing who the antagonist was without foreshadowing anything. It was a torture!!<br><br>To top it all off this book is indeed a cliffhanger<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482276024ra/21500389.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WHY JANE!??! WHY!?!?!<br>The author is able to encompass a certain darkness within her writing quite seamlessly and I have noticed this skill in another book of hers as well. I am a fan!<br><br><b> The Bad: Writing.. </b> <br>It felt like a JUMBLED MESS ALL THE TIME, I understand that she is writing a suspenseful story but even the phrasing and the flow of the book was giving me a whiplash. There were too many instances where misinterpretation would be bound to happen and I had to spend too much time rereading the situation. It was hard to understand the exact meaning and plot progress which lead to lots of confusion.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418715886ra/12881963.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b> The Good: Characterization </b><br>I was thoroughly impressed with the backstory of our h, the author convinced me of the pain and trauma felt by her. I was able to connect with the h through all of the situations presented before her.<br>I felt the steady backbone she provided throughout the story. For the first time in YA I saw that the main character was actually questioning fate and the forced situation that was thrust upon her.<br>I definitely saw the distinction between Miro/Quillan and Silas characters, they were well fleshed out and engaged me as a reader thoroughly. <br><br><b> The Bad: Characterization </b><br>Nonetheless, I can not say that I was convinced of Seraph's badassery just yet. I would like to see her take proactive action.<br>Noah and Cabe started to blend together to me although I am not sure whether it was purposeful by the author or not.<br>I also felt that as readers we were kept in the dark regarding the motivations of the antagonist for far too long without any hints. It felt disjointed as the characters went around in circles without reaching any conclusion to the main conflict.<br><br><b> The Good: Relationships </b><br>I have read previous books with menage and many partners but they were all erotic (not that I have a problem with that). Although, this book really dwelled into the true meaning and different facets of the relationship in a really unique and realistic way.<br>The tension/chemistry/connection experienced between the main characters was marvellous! I am the biggest self appointed angst-whore-reader any author will find so I was all about it!!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1409591943ra/10996346.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> The Bad: Relationships </b><br>While I may be an angst-whore the author still needed to feed me the crumbs to keep the feeling alive. During certain times of the plot I did not understand the need for secrecy which lead to the disconnect within MC's.<br>I would like to see a bigger arc within their relationship a result or consequence of the situations around them. It felt stagnant to me.<br><br><b> Most importantly </b> I want action <s> as in WHY aren't they FUCKING? </s><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487557330ra/22025985.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Finally, <s> (I know I would make my lit prof proud if they ever read this analysis) </s><br>I did like this book in spite of its faults..I mean it is obvious as I binge read the first 2 in the series without a stop! So I would recommend it to others if you have some patience and a passion for some paranormal. <br><br><i> I have decided to give this book its 4th star for the polyamorous relationship! </i><br><s> YES! I AM AWARE THAT I AM BIASED that's why it's called MY OPINION AND NOT YOURS! </s></span>
  <a data-text-id="17956259899122829036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1395783856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1395783856" />
    <a title="Harrison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41201064-harrison"><img alt="Harrison" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1395783856?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Harrison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Harrison" href="/user/show/41201064-harrison">Harrison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1395783856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16475764711709047246">This book truly exceeded my expectations. Gripping from the very first scene. The quality of writing was superb, the descriptions of the characters moving and the imagery vivid. From the very opening lines I knew this was gonna be one hell of a good book. <br/>I must admit I had a hard time getting my head around four men being so heavily interested in this one girl with their unusually complicated relationships with her, but it made for a whole new level of suspense I had not encountered before in a</span>
  <span id="freeText16475764711709047246" style="display:none">This book truly exceeded my expectations. Gripping from the very first scene. The quality of writing was superb, the descriptions of the characters moving and the imagery vivid. From the very opening lines I knew this was gonna be one hell of a good book. <br />I must admit I had a hard time getting my head around four men being so heavily interested in this one girl with their unusually complicated relationships with her, but it made for a whole new level of suspense I had not encountered before in any novel. I simply could not put the book down. The Bond between Seraph and the four men is complex to say the least, but left me yearning to find out more about them. I guess we shall have a better idea once the sequel is out. The Zevgheri’s seem to be a very alluring race, of which Seraph seems to exemplify their unparalleled beauty and power. I liked the strong, impressionable characterisation of Noah, Cabe, Silas and Quillan but was constantly trying to figure out what was the whole deal with them and the Zevgheri! The sinister stalker creepomaniac blew me away, and so did Poison with her supercharged mischievousness.<br />Being an artist myself I absolutely LOVED the way Seraph would paint and her paintings would come to life. Incredible concept. <br />I would recommend this book to anyone who has any interest in romance, or fantasy, but with a reminder that it does get pretty intense and one should cancel all activities for the next 72 hrs as I did.<br />I am so relieved to find a book which breaks the norms of modern romance novels where the protagonist female character is no super duper know it all chick from the very start. Seraph is seen to be growing as a person, maturing into someone beautiful and potent, powerful and delicate all the same. There is nothing fickle or vain about her, or for that matter, about any of the four guys, and that creates for a deeper bond between them. Silas, proved to be undoubtedly the most appealing and yet the most diabolical love interest and someone whose secrets I beg the author to uncover in the next book.<br />I am really curious to find out what is going to happen with the four and how their relationships will pan out, let alone what happens with stalker guy. Cannot wait for the next release!<br />PS I loved the name Seraph.<br />I also think Silas, Tariq and Noah are wonderfully named as well. Well suited to their personalities, in my opinion. It’s a seriously well thought out book. Cannot wait for a sequel. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16475764711709047246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2447529297" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447529297" />
    <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue"><img alt="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390185382p2/4659650.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447529297?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)" href="/user/show/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue">Jen (The Starry-Eyed Revue)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36271664-charcoal-tears">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=kindle-unlimited">kindle-unlimited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=audible-romance-package">audible-romance-package</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=reverse-harem">reverse-harem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=paranormal-other">paranormal-other</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4659650-jen-the-starry-eyed-revue?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447529297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3947952956939411059"><b>SERAPH BLACK series - </b>This one is definitely more YA, with god-like gifts being bestowed upon mere mortals. It's not really mythology-based, but the Zev society hidden among humans does have its own mythology, if that makes sense. The summaries for these books just do not do them justice. They are a thing unto themselves and it only gets crazier as the series progresses.<br/><br/><b>Charcoal Tears</b> - So, after trying several reverse harem stories and ultimately being disappointed by each, I wasn't expecting m</span>
  <span id="freeText3947952956939411059" style="display:none"><b>SERAPH BLACK series - </b>This one is definitely more YA, with god-like gifts being bestowed upon mere mortals. It's not really mythology-based, but the Zev society hidden among humans does have its own mythology, if that makes sense. The summaries for these books just do not do them justice. They are a thing unto themselves and it only gets crazier as the series progresses.<br /><br /><b>Charcoal Tears</b> - So, after trying several reverse harem stories and ultimately being disappointed by each, I wasn't expecting much from this book. Especially since it was considered young adult and I was searching for something more akin to the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/231797-power-of-five" rel="nofollow noopener">Alex Lidell series</a> I read last month. But <i>Charcoal Tears</i> was really quite good! The characterization, the plotting, the pace, the lingering questions...all were fantastic and kept me captivated. I wasn't even through with this first book before I was downloading the rest of the series on Kindle Unlimited. Truthfully, I read these books back-to-back-to-back over the course of the weekend, so I can't really differentiate between them at this point, but they're good, <i>really</i> good: humorous while also tackling some really awful truths, well-written, and super-intriguing.  🌟🌟🌟🌟<br /><br /><b>Watercolor Smile</b> - I think I suspected who the Messenger was in the first book, but this book cemented it for me. However, that made the creepy rhymes and cruel deaths no less sinister. The Messenger's efforts <i>did</i> manage to push Seraph and her bondmates closer together, though, and <i>this </i>is how I want to see this type of romance play out: getting to know one another, forming connections, and <i>then</i> moving on to the physical stuff. But it's been pretty tame so far, which I appreciate because YAY the tight-knit closeness of this group but which I also loathe because FOUR BROTHERS. Ahem. 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br /><br /><b>Lead Heart</b> - In this third installment, you could just feel Seph's solace, the sense of betrayal and her inability to trust pretty much anyone. It just leaks off the pages. But you can't blame her, considering everything she's been through. I think <i>Lead Heart</i> is a very apropos title. Big changes in this book, but it's late in the series and I feel like anything I say might be spoilery. Just...if you've made it this far, you've got to read the final book. 🌟🌟🌟🌟<br /><br /><b>A Portrait of Pain</b> - I am so, SO glad this was a completed series when I stumbled upon it. The only ones I've seemed to enjoy lately are those that are unfinished series and it's driving me crazy. Constant book hangover is no way to live one's life. <i>Anyway</i>...this final book was a big ole box of WTFs. The reveals! The sexy times! The near-constant refrain of <i>how is this even going to work</i>?!? I read it in one sitting, as soon as I finished <i>Lead Heart</i> and though I think the author maybe jumped the shark a bit here in this final book, I still maintain that it was a pretty great series on the whole. I did think it was odd that the author chose to showcase the mates voices in this last book, though. It was the first time you got to read from their perspectives, if I remember correctly, but it felt almost unnecessary at this point. The author did such a great job of introducing each Atma (mate) from the beginning and it felt understood how each would be feeling in the moment, so close were their bonds to Seph. Oh, and also, #TeamMiro. :D (I can't be the only one who likes the responsible leader. It always feels like that guy gets the shaft (ha!) because he's always putting duty above everything else.) 🌟🌟🌟🌟</span>
  <a data-text-id="3947952956939411059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
